"هِيهْ، وَمَا وَافِدُ عَادٍ؟ " -وَهُوَ أَعْلَمُ بِالْحَدِيثِ مِنْهُ، وَلَكِنْ يَسْتَطْعِمُهُ -قُلْتُ: إِنْ عَادًا قُحِطُوا فَبَعَثُوا وَافِدًا لَهُمْ يُقَالُ لَهُ: قَيل، فَمَرَّ بِمُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ بَكْرٍ، فَأَقَامَ عِنْدَهُ شَهْرًا يَسْقِيهِ الْخَمْرَ وَتُغَنِّيهِ جَارِيَتَانِ يُقَالُ لَهُمَا "الْجَرَادَتَانِ"-فَلَمَّا مَضَى الشَّهْرُ خَرَجَ إِلَى جِبَالِ مَهْرة فقال: اللهم، إِنَّكَ تَعْلَمُ أَنِّي لَمْ أَجِئْ إِلَى مَرِيضٍ فَأُدَاوِيهِ، وَلَا إِلَى أَسِيرٍ فَأُفَادِيهِ، اللَّهُمَّ اسْقِ عَادًا مَا كُنْتَ تَسْقِيهِ. فَمَرَّتْ بِهِ سَحَّابَاتٌ سُودُ، فَنُودِيَ مِنْهَا: "اخْتَرْ"، فَأَوْمَأَ إِلَى سَحَابَةٍ مِنْهَا سَوْدَاءَ، فَنُودِيَ مِنْهَا: "خُذْهَا رَمَادًا رِمْدِدًا ، لَا تُبْقِي مِنْ عَادٍ أَحَدًا". قَالَ: فَمَا بَلَغَنِي أَنَّهُ أُرْسِلَ عَلَيْهِمْ مِنَ الرِّيحِ إِلَّا كَقَدْرِ مَا يَجْرِي فِي خَاتَمِي هَذَا، حَتَّى هَلَكُوا-قَالَ أَبُو وَائِلٍ: وَصَدَقَ -وَكَانَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ وَالرَّجُلُ إِذَا بَعَثُوا وَافِدًا لَهُمْ قَالُوا: "لَا تَكُنْ كَوَافِدِ عَادٍ".

رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ فِي سُورَةِ "الْأَعْرَافِ" .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا هَارُونُ بْنُ مَعْرُوفٍ، أَخْبَرَنَا ابْنُ وَهْبٍ، أَخْبَرَنَا عَمْرٌو: أَنَّ أَبَا النَّضْرِ حَدَّثَهُ عَنْ سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ يَسَارٍ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ: مَا رَأَيْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ مُسْتَجْمِعًا ضَاحِكًا حَتَّى أَرَى مِنْهُ لَهَوَاتِهِ، إِنَّمَا كَانَ يَتَبَسَّمُ. قَالَتْ: وَكَانَ إِذَا رَأَى غَيْمًا -أَوْ رِيحًا-عُرِفَ ذَلِكَ فِي وَجْهِهِ، قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، النَّاسُ إِذَا رَأَوُا الْغَيْمَ فَرِحُوا رَجَاءَ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيهِ الْمَطَرُ، وَأَرَاكَ إِذَا رَأَيْتَهُ عَرَفْتُ فِي وَجْهِكَ الْكَرَاهِيَةَ؟ فَقَالَ: "يَا عَائِشَةُ، مَا يُؤَمِّنُنِي أَنْ يَكُونَ فِيهِ عَذَابٌ، قَدْ عُذِّبَ قَوْمٌ بِالرِّيحِ، وَقَدْ رَأَى قَوْمٌ الْعَذَابَ فَقَالُوا: هَذَا عَارِضٌ مُمْطِرُنَا". وَأَخْرَجَاهُ مِنْ حَدِيثِ ابْنِ وَهْبٍ .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ، عَنْ سُفْيَانَ، عَنْ الْمِقْدَامِ بْنِ شُرَيْحٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ كَانَ إِذَا رَأَى نَاشِئًا فِي أُفُقٍ مِنْ آفَاقِ السَّمَاءِ، تَرَكَ عَمَلَهُ، وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ، ثُمَّ يَقُولُ: "اللَّهُمَّ، إِنِّي أَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّ مَا فِيهِ" . فَإِنْ كَشَفَهُ اللَّهُ حَمِدَ اللَّهَ، وَإِنْ أَمْطَرَتْ قَالَ: "اللَّهُمَّ، صَيِّبًا نَافِعًا" .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ مُسْلِمٌ فِي صَحِيحِهِ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو الطَّاهِرِ، أَخْبَرَنَا ابْنُ وَهْبٍ، سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ جُرَيْجٍ يُحَدِّثُ عَنْ عَطَاءِ بْنِ أَبِي رَبَاحٍ، عَنْ عَائِشَةَ قَالَتْ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وسلم إِذَا عَصَفَتِ الرِّيحُ قَالَ: "اللَّهُمَّ، إِنِّي أَسْأَلُكَ خَيْرَهَا، وَخَيْرَ مَا فِيهَا، وَخَيْرَ مَا أُرْسِلَتْ بِهِ، وَأَعُوذُ بِكَ مِنْ شَرِّهَا، وَشَرِّ مَا فِيهَا، وَشَرِّ مَا أُرْسِلَتْ بِهِ". قَالَتْ: وَإِذَا تَخَيَّلت السَّمَاءُ تَغَيَّرَ لَوْنُهُ، وَخَرَجَ وَدَخَلَ، وَأَقْبَلَ وَأَدْبَرَ، فَإِذَا مَطَرَتْ سُرِّيَ عَنْهُ، فَعَرَفَتْ ذَلِكَ عَائِشَةُ، فَسَأَلَتْهُ، فَقَالَ: "لَعَلَّهُ يَا عَائِشَةُ كَمَا قَالَ قَوْمُ عَادٍ: ﴿فَلَمَّا رَأَوْهُ عَارِضًا مُسْتَقْبِلَ أَوْدِيَتِهِمْ قَالُوا هَذَا عَارِضٌ مُمْطِرُنَا﴾ .

وَقَدْ ذَكَرْنَا قِصَّةَ هَلَاكِ عَادٍ فِي سُورَتَيِ "الْأَعْرَافِ وَهُودٍ" بما أغنى عن إعادته هاهنا، ولله الْحَمْدُ وَالْمِنَّةُ.

وَقَالَ الطَّبَرَانِيُّ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدَانُ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ، حَدَّثَنَا إِسْمَاعِيلُ بْنُ زَكَرِيَّا الْكُوفِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو مَالِكٍ، عَنْ مُسْلِمٍ الْمُلَائِيِّ، عَنْ مُجَاهِدٍ وَسَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: "مَا فُتِحَ عَلَى عَادٍ مِنَ الرِّيحِ إِلَّا مِثْلُ مَوْضِعِ الْخَاتَمِ، ثُمَّ أُرْسِلَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ [فَحَمَلَتْهُمُ] الْبَدْوَ إِلَى الْحَضَرِ فَلَمَّا رَآهَا أَهْلُ الْحَضَرِ قَالُوا: هَذَا عَارَضٌ مُمْطِرُنَا مُسْتَقْبَلُ أَوْدِيَتِنَا. وَكَانَ أَهْلُ الْبَوَادِي فِيهَا، فَأُلْقِي أَهْلُ الْبَادِيَةِ عَلَى أَهْلِ الْحَاضِرَةِ حَتَّى هَلَكُوا. قَالَ: عَتَتْ عَلَى خُزَّانِهَا حَتَّى خَرَجَتْ مِنْ خِلَالِ الْأَبْوَابِ " .

---

## 46:26-28 — verses 26-28 (shared commentary)

### Translation

The Almighty says: We had indeed established the preceding nations firmly in the world with wealth and children, and We gave them of that what We have not given you the like of, nor anything close to it. {And We had granted them hearing, sight, and hearts, but neither their hearing, nor their sight, nor their hearts availed them in anything, since they used to deny the signs of Allah, and there befell them what they used to mock.} That is: the punishment and the exemplary retribution which they used to disbelieve in and regard as impossible to occur closed in upon them and surrounded them. That is: so beware, you who are being addressed, lest you be like them, so that there befalls you the like of what befell them of punishment in this world and the next.

His saying: {And We had indeed destroyed the towns around you} means: the people of Mecca. Allah had destroyed the nations that disbelieved the messengers among those around it, such as 'Ad, who were in al-Ahqaf near Hadramawt, close to Yemen, and Thamud, whose dwellings were between them and the Levant. Likewise Saba', who were the people of Yemen, and Madyan, which lay on their route and path toward Gaza. Likewise the lake of the people of Lot, which they also used to pass by.

His saying: {And We had diversified the signs} means: We made them clear and evident, {so that they might return. Why then did not those whom they had taken besides Allah as offerings, as gods, help them?} That is: why did these gods not help them at the time they needed them? {Rather, they vanished from them.} That is: rather, they departed from them at the very moment they were most in need of them. {And that was their falsehood} that is, their lie, {and what they used to fabricate}, that is, their fabrication in taking these as gods. They had indeed failed and lost in their worship of them and their reliance upon them.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

يَقُولُ تَعَالَى: وَلَقَدْ مَكَّنَّا الْأُمَمَ السَّالِفَةَ فِي الدُّنْيَا مِنَ الْأَمْوَالِ وَالْأَوْلَادِ، وَأَعْطَيْنَاهُمْ مِنْهَا مَا لَمْ نُعْطِكُمْ مِثْلَهُ وَلَا قَرِيبًا مِنْهُ، ﴿وَجَعَلْنَا لَهُمْ سَمْعًا وَأَبْصَارًا وَأَفْئِدَةً فَمَا أَغْنَى عَنْهُمْ سَمْعُهُمْ وَلا أَبْصَارُهُمْ وَلا أَفْئِدَتُهُمْ مِنْ شَيْءٍ إِذْ كَانُوا يَجْحَدُونَ بِآيَاتِ اللَّهِ وَحَاقَ بِهِمْ مَا كَانُوا بِهِ يَسْتَهْزِئُونَ﴾ أَيْ: وَأَحَاطَ بِهِمُ الْعَذَابُ وَالنَّكَالُ الَّذِي كَانُوا يُكَذِّبُونَ بِهِ وَيَسْتَبْعِدُونَ وُقُوعَهُ، أَيْ: فَاحْذَرُوا أَيُّهَا الْمُخَاطَبُونَ أَنْ تَكُونُوا مِثْلَهُمْ، فَيُصِيبَكُمْ مِثْلُ مَا أَصَابَهُمْ مِنَ الْعَذَابِ فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْآخِرَةِ.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَلَقَدْ أَهْلَكْنَا مَا حَوْلَكُمْ مِنَ الْقُرَى﴾ يَعْنِي: أَهْلَ مَكَّةَ، قَدْ أَهْلَكَ اللَّهُ الْأُمَمَ الْمُكَذِّبَةَ بِالرُّسُلِ مِمَّا حَوْلَهَا كَعَادٍ، وَكَانُوا بِالْأَحْقَافِ بِحَضْرَمَوْتَ عِنْدَ الْيَمَنِ وَثَمُودَ، وَكَانَتْ مَنَازِلُهُمْ بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ الشَّامِ، وَكَذَلِكَ سَبَأٌ وَهُمْ أَهْلُ الْيَمَنِ، وَمَدْيَنُ وَكَانَتْ فِي طَرِيقِهِمْ وَمَمَرِّهِمْ إِلَى غَزَّةَ، وَكَذَلِكَ بُحَيْرَةُ قَوْمِ لُوطٍ، كَانُوا يَمُرُّونَ بِهَا أَيْضًا.

* *

وَقَوْلُهُ: ﴿وَصَرَّفْنَا الآيَاتِ﴾ أَيْ: بَيَّنَّاهَا وَوَضَّحْنَاهَا، ﴿لَعَلَّهُمْ يَرْجِعُونَ فَلَوْلا نَصَرَهُمُ الَّذِينَ اتَّخَذُوا مِنْ دُونِ اللَّهِ قُرْبَانًا آلِهَة﴾ أَيْ: فَهَلَّا نَصَرُوهُمْ عِنْدَ احْتِيَاجِهِمْ إِلَيْهِمْ، ﴿بَلْ ضَلُّوا عَنْهُمْ﴾ أَيْ: بَلْ ذَهَبُوا عَنْهُمْ أَحْوَجَ مَا كَانُوا إِلَيْهِمْ، ﴿وَذَلِكَ إِفْكُهُمْ﴾ أَيْ: كَذِبُهُمْ، ﴿وَمَا كَانُوا يَفْتَرُونَ﴾ أَيْ: وَافْتِرَاؤُهُمْ فِي اتِّخَاذِهِمْ إِيَّاهُمْ آلِهَةً، وَقَدْ خَابُوا وَخَسِرُوا في عبادتهم لها، واعتمادهم عليها.

---

## 46:29-32 — verses 29-32 (shared commentary)

### Translation

Imam Ahmad said: Sufyan told us, Amr told us: I heard Ikrimah, from al-Zubayr, [commenting on]: {And when We turned toward you a group of the jinn, listening to the Qur'an}, he said: at Nakhlah, while the Messenger of God ﷺ was praying the last night prayer (al-'isha' al-akhirah), {they almost became a compacted mass upon him} [al-Jinn: 19]. Sufyan said: al-libad means them piled one upon another, like felt (libad) layered one upon another.

Ahmad alone transmitted this. It will come later through the narration of Ibn Jarir, from Ikrimah, from Ibn Abbas: that they were seven from the jinn of Nasibin.

Imam Ahmad also said: Affan told us, Abu Awanah told us (ch) and the hafiz Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi said in his book "Dala'il al-Nubuwwah": Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Ahmad ibn Abdan informed us, Ahmad ibn Ubayd al-Saffar informed us, Isma'il al-Qadi told us, Musaddad informed us, Abu Awanah told us, from Abu Bishr, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas, who said: The Messenger of God ﷺ neither recited to the jinn nor saw them. The Messenger of God ﷺ set out with a group of his companions heading toward the market of Ukaz. At that time a barrier had been placed between the devils and the news of heaven, and shooting stars (shuhub) were sent against them. So the devils returned to their people and said: What is the matter with you? They said: A barrier has been placed between us and the news of heaven, and shooting stars have been sent against us. They said: Nothing could have placed a barrier between you and the news of heaven except something that has newly occurred. So spread out across the easts and wests of the earth and see what this thing is that has come between you and the news of heaven. So they set out, spreading across the easts and wests of the earth, seeking to find out what this thing was that had come between them and the news of heaven. Then that group which had headed toward Tihamah returned to the Messenger of God ﷺ, who was at Nakhlah heading toward the market of Ukaz, while he was leading his companions in the dawn prayer. When they heard the Qur'an, they listened attentively to it, and said: This, by God, is what has come between you and the news of heaven. Then, when they returned to their people, they said: O our people, we have heard a wondrous Qur'an, which guides to right conduct, so we have believed in it, and we will never associate anyone with our Lord. And God, exalted is He, revealed to His Prophet: {Say: It has been revealed to me that a group of the jinn listened} [al-Jinn: 1]. What was revealed to him was only the speech of the jinn [reporting what had happened].

Al-Bukhari narrated it from Musaddad in a similar wording, and Muslim narrated it from Shayban ibn Farrukh, from Abu Awanah, with the same chain. Al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated it in their books of tafsir, from the hadith of Abu Awanah.

Imam Ahmad also said: Abu Ahmad told us, Isra'il told us, from Abu Ishaq, from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas, who said: The jinn used to listen to the revelation (wahy). They would hear a word and add ten more to it, so that what they had heard would be true, and what they added would be false. Before that, stars were not shot at [the jinn]. When the Messenger of God ﷺ was sent, none of them would go to his usual seat without being struck by a shooting star that burned whatever it hit. So they complained of this to Iblis, who said: This can only be because of some matter that has newly occurred. So he dispatched his troops, and they found the Prophet ﷺ praying between the two mountains of Nakhlah. They came to him and informed him, so he said: This is the newly occurring matter that has occurred on earth.

Al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i narrated it in the tafsir books of their two Sunan collections, from the hadith of Isra'il with the same chain, and al-Tirmidhi said: hasan sahih (good, sound).

Likewise Ayyub narrated it from Sa'id ibn Jubayr, from Ibn Abbas. And al-Awfi likewise narrated it from Ibn Abbas as well, with a similarly lengthy wording. Al-Hasan al-Basri said similarly: that he, peace be upon him, was not aware of their affair until God revealed to him news of them.

Muhammad ibn Ishaq mentioned, from Yazid ibn Ruman, from Muhammad ibn Ka'b al-Qurazi, the story of the Messenger of God's ﷺ going out to al-Ta'if and his calling them to God, mighty and majestic is He, and their refusal of him. He related the story at length, and included that beautiful supplication: "O God, to You I complain of the weakness of my strength and the paucity of my resources..." to its end. He said: When he turned away from them, he spent the night at Nakhlah, and that night he recited from the Qur'an, and the jinn of the people of Nasibin heard it.

This is sound (sahih), but his statement that "the jinn's listening was on that night" requires scrutiny, because the jinn's listening occurred at the very beginning of the revelation, as indicated by the aforementioned hadith of Ibn Abbas, whereas his, peace be upon him, going out to al-Ta'if occurred after the death of his uncle, and that was a year or two before the Hijrah, as established by Ibn Ishaq and others. [And God knows best.]

Abu Bakr ibn Abi Shaybah said: Abu Ahmad al-Zubayri told us, Sufyan told us, from Asim, from Zirr, from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, who said: They descended upon the Prophet ﷺ while he was reciting the Qur'an at the valley floor of Nakhlah. When they heard him, they said: Be silent and listen. He said: Hush. They numbered nine, one of whom was Zawba'ah. So God, mighty and majestic is He, revealed: {And when We turned toward you a group of the jinn, listening to the Qur'an, and when they were present at it, they said, Be silent and listen. Then when it was concluded, they turned back to their people as warners} up to: {manifest error}.

This report, together with the first one from the narration of Ibn Abbas, indicates that the Messenger of God ﷺ was not aware of their presence on this occasion, and that they merely listened to his recitation, then returned to their people. After that, delegations of them came to him in successive groups, people after people, and company after company, as the reports and traditions concerning that will come in their proper places, which we will present here, God willing, and in Him is trust.

As for what al-Bukhari and Muslim both narrated, from Abu Qudamah Ubaydullah ibn Sa'id al-Sarakhsi, from Abu Usamah Hammad ibn Usamah, from Mis'ar ibn Kidam, from Ma'n ibn Abd al-Rahman, who said: I heard my father say: I asked Masruq: Who informed the Prophet ﷺ on the night when they listened to the Qur'an? He said: Your father told me, meaning Ibn Mas'ud, that a tree informed him of them. It is possible that this refers to the first occasion, and would constitute an affirmation that takes precedence over Ibn Abbas's denial. And it is possible that this refers to one of the later occasions, and God knows best. It is also possible that it occurred on the first occasion, but that he was not aware of them during their listening until the tree informed him of them, that is, made known to him that they had listened, and God knows best.

The hafiz al-Bayhaqi said: What Ibn Abbas, may God be pleased with him, related pertains only to the first time the jinn heard the recitation of the Messenger of God ﷺ and learned of his condition. At that time he did not recite to them nor did he see them. After that, a summoner (da'i) of the jinn came to him, and he recited the Qur'an to them and called them to God, mighty and majestic is He, as Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, may God be pleased with him, related.

Mention of the narration from him regarding that:

Imam Ahmad said: Isma'il ibn Ibrahim told us, Dawud told us, from al-Sha'bi, and Ibn Abi Za'idah, Dawud informed us, from al-Sha'bi, from Alqamah, who said: I said to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud: Did any of you accompany the Messenger of God ﷺ on the night of the jinn? He said: None of us accompanied him, but we lost track of him one night in Mecca, and we said: Has he been assassinated? Has he been carried off? What has happened to him? He said: We spent the worst night that people ever spent. Then, at the approach of dawn, or he said: during the pre dawn hours, there he suddenly was, coming from the direction of Hira. We said: O Messenger of God, and they related to him what state they had been in. He said: "A summoner of the jinn came to me, so I went to them and recited to them." He said: Then he set off and showed us their traces and the traces of their fires. He said, and al-Sha'bi said: They asked him for provision. Amir said: They asked him at Mecca, and they were from the jinn of the Peninsula (al-Jazirah). So he said: "Every bone over which the name of God has been mentioned will fall into your hands with more meat on it than it had before, and every piece of dung or droppings will be fodder for your animals." He said: "So do not use them for cleansing after relieving yourselves, for they are the provision of your brethren among the jinn."

Muslim likewise narrated it in his Sahih, from Ali ibn Hujr, from Isma'il ibn Ulayyah, with a similar wording.

Muslim also said: Muhammad ibn al-Muthanna narrated to us, Abd al-A'la narrated to us, Dawud (that is, Ibn Abi Hind) narrated to us, from Amir who said: I asked Alqamah, "Did Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, witness the night of the jinn with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ?" He said: Alqamah replied: I asked Ibn Mas'ud myself; I said, "Did any of you witness the night of the jinn with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ?" He said: No, but we were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ one night and we lost track of him. We searched for him in the valleys and the mountain passes, and we said, "Has he been snatched away? Has he been murdered?" He said: We spent the worst night any people ever spent, and when morning came, there he was, coming from the direction of Hira. He said: We said, "O Messenger of Allah, we lost you and searched for you but could not find you, and we spent the worst night any people ever spent." He said, "A caller of the jinn came to me, so I went with them and recited the Qur'an to them." He said: He took us and showed us their tracks and the traces of their fires. They had asked him for provision, so he said, "Every bone over which the name of Allah has been mentioned falls into your hands with the most abundant meat possible, and every piece of dung or droppings is fodder for your animals." The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said, "So do not cleanse yourselves with these two things, for they are the food of your brethren."

Another chain, from Ibn Mas'ud: Abu Ja'far ibn Jarir said: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman narrated to me, my uncle narrated to me, Yunus narrated to me, from al-Zuhri, from Ubayd Allah ibn Abd Allah, that Ibn Mas'ud said: I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say, "I spent the night reciting a quarter (of the Qur'an) to the jinn at al-Hajun."

Another chain, in which it is stated that he was with him on the night of the jinn. Ibn Jarir, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Ahmad ibn Abd al-Rahman ibn Wahb narrated to me, my uncle Abd Allah ibn Wahb narrated to us, Yunus informed me, from Ibn Shihab, from Abu Uthman ibn Sannah al-Khuza'i, who was one of the people of Syria, that Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said to his companions while he was in Mecca, "Whoever among you would like to be present for the matter of the jinn tonight, let him do so." None of them came except me. He said: We set off until, when we were in the upper part of Mecca, he drew a line for me with his foot, then commanded me to sit within it. Then he went on until he stood, and he began reciting the Qur'an. Numerous black forms enveloped him, coming between me and him, until I could not hear his voice. Then they began breaking apart like pieces of cloud departing, until a group of them remained. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ finished at dawn, then he went off to relieve himself, then came to me and said, "What became of the group?" I said, "They are there, O Messenger of Allah." So he gave them a bone and dung as provision, then he forbade anyone from cleansing himself with dung or bone.

Ibn Jarir also related it from Muhammad ibn Abd Allah ibn Abd al-Hakam, from Abu Zur'ah Wahb Allah ibn Rashid, from Yunus ibn Yazid al-Ayli, with the same content.

Al-Bayhaqi related it in al-Dala'il, from the hadith of Abd Allah ibn Salih, the scribe of al-Layth, from al-Layth, from Yunus, with the same content.

Ishaq ibn Rahawayh related it from Jarir, from Qabus ibn Abi Zabyan, from his father, from Ibn Mas'ud, mentioning something similar to what preceded.

The hafiz Abu Nu'aym related it, by way of Musa ibn Ubaydah, from Sa'id ibn al-Harith, from Abu al-Mu'alla, from Ibn Mas'ud, mentioning something similar as well.

Another chain: Abu Nu'aym said: Abu Bakr ibn Malik narrated to us, Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal narrated to us, my father narrated to me, he said: Affan and Ikrimah narrated to us, they said: Mu'tamir narrated to us, he said: My father said: Abu Tamimah narrated to me, from Amr, and perhaps he said al-Bikali, who narrated it, from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ asked me to follow him, so we set off until we came to such and such a place. He drew a line for me and said, "Stay within the middle of this; do not go out of it, for if you go out of it you will perish." He mentioned the hadith at length, and it contains considerable gharabah (unusualness/singularity in transmission).

Another chain: Ibn Jarir said: Ibn Abd al-A'la narrated to us, Ibn Thawr narrated to us, from Ma'mar, from Yahya ibn Abi Kathir, from Abd Allah ibn Amr ibn Ghaylan al-Thaqafi, that he said to Ibn Mas'ud: I have been told that you were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the delegation of the jinn. He said: Yes. He said: How was it? So he mentioned the whole hadith, and mentioned that the Prophet ﷺ drew a line around him and said, "Do not leave it." He mentioned something like a black dust cloud that enveloped the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and he (Ibn Mas'ud) was frightened three times, until, when it was near dawn, the Prophet ﷺ came to me and said, "Did you sleep?" I said, "No, by Allah, and I was several times on the verge of calling out to people for help, until I heard you striking them with your staff, saying, 'Sit down.'" He said, "If you had gone out, I could not have guaranteed that some of them would not have snatched you away." Then he said, "Did you see anything?" I said, "Yes, I saw black men wrapped in white garments." He said, "Those are the jinn of Nasibin. They asked me for provision, meaning food, so I provided them with every discarded bone, or dung, or droppings." I said, "O Messenger of Allah, what good does that do for them?" He said, "They find no bone but that they find upon it the meat it had on the day it was eaten, nor any dung but that they find in it the grain it contained on the day it was consumed. So let none of you, when he comes out from relieving himself, cleanse himself with a bone, dung, or droppings."

Another chain: The hafiz Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi said: Abu Abd al-Rahman al-Sulami and Abu Nasr ibn Qatadah informed us, they said: Abu Muhammad Yahya ibn Mansur al-Qadi informed us, Abu Abd Allah Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Bushanji narrated to us, Rawh ibn Salah narrated to us, Musa ibn Ali ibn Rabah narrated to us, from his father, from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ asked me to follow him and said, "A group of the jinn, fifteen, sons of brothers and cousins, are coming to me tonight, so I will recite the Qur'an to them." So I went with him to the place he intended. He drew a line for me and made me sit within it, and said to me, "Do not leave this." So I spent the night in it until the Messenger of Allah ﷺ came to me at dawn with a discarded bone and a charred piece of dung in his hand, and said to me, "When you go to relieve yourself, do not cleanse yourself with any of these." He said: When morning came I said, "I must know for certain where the Messenger of Allah ﷺ stood." So I went and saw the site where sixty camels had knelt.

Another chain: Al-Bayhaqi said: Abu Abd Allah al-Hafiz informed us, Abu al-Abbas al-Asamm informed us, al-Abbas ibn Muhammad al-Duri narrated to us, Uthman ibn Umar narrated to us, from al-Mustamirr ibn al-Rayyan, from Abu al-Jawza', from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, who said: I went with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the jinn, until he came to al-Hajun. He drew a line for me, then went forward to them, and they crowded around him. A chief of theirs, called Wardan, said, "I will drive them away from you." He said, "No one can protect me from Allah."

Another chain: Imam Ahmad said: Abd al-Razzaq narrated to us, Sufyan narrated to us, from Abu Fazarah al-Absi, Abu Zayd, the freedman of Amr ibn Hurayth, narrated to us, from Ibn Mas'ud, who said: On the night of the jinn, the Prophet ﷺ said to me, "Do you have water with you?" I said, "I have no water with me, but I have a small skin containing date-wine." The Prophet said, "A good date and pure water," and he performed ablution with it.

Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and Ibn Majah related it from the hadith of Abu Zayd, with the same content.

Another chain: Ahmad said: Yahya ibn Ishaq narrated to us, Ibn Lahi'ah informed us, from Qays ibn al-Hajjaj, from Hanash al-San'ani, from Ibn Abbas, from Abd Allah ibn Mas'ud, that he was with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the jinn. The Messenger of Allah said, "O Abd Allah, do you have water with you?" He said, "I have date-wine in a small skin." He said, "Pour it on me." So he performed ablution with it, and the Prophet ﷺ said, "O Abd Allah, a drink and a purifier."

Ahmad alone related this from this route, and al-Daraqutni recorded it by another chain from Ibn Mas'ud, with the same content.

Another chain: Imam Ahmad said: Abd al-Razzaq narrated to us, my father informed me, from Mina, from Abd Allah, who said: I was with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the delegation of the jinn. When he finished, he sighed, so I said, "What is wrong with you?" He said, "My death has been announced to me, O Ibn Mas'ud."

This is what I saw in the Musnad, in abbreviated form. The Hafiz Abu Nu'aym related it in his book "Dala'il al-Nubuwwah," saying: Sulayman ibn Ahmad ibn Ayyub told us, Ishaq ibn Ibrahim told us, and Abu Bakr ibn Malik told us, 'Abd Allah ibn Ahmad ibn Hanbal told us, my father told us, both saying: 'Abd al-Razzaq told us, from his father, from Mina, from Ibn Mas'ud who said: I was with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the delegation of the jinn, and he sighed. I said, "What is wrong, O Messenger of Allah?" He said, "My death has been announced to me, O Ibn Mas'ud." I said, "Appoint a successor." He said, "Who?" I said, "Abu Bakr." He remained silent, then went on for a while and sighed again. I said, "What is the matter, may my father and mother be sacrificed for you, O Messenger of Allah?" He said, "My death has been announced to me, O Ibn Mas'ud." I said, "Appoint a successor." He said, "Who?" I said, "Umar [ibn al-Khattab]." He remained silent, then went on for a while, then sighed and I said, "What is the matter?" He said, "My death has been announced to me." I said, "Then appoint a successor." He ﷺ said, "Who?" I said, "Ali ibn Abi Talib." He ﷺ said, "By Him in whose hand is my soul, if they obey him they will all enter Paradise together, every one of them."

This is a hadith that is very gharib (singular), and it is more fitting that it not be considered preserved. Even granting its soundness, it is apparent that this would be after their delegation to him in Madinah, as we shall relate, for it was at that later time, when Makkah was conquered and people and jinn alike entered the religion of Allah in throngs, that the surah {When the help of Allah comes and the victory, and you see the people entering the religion of Allah in throngs, then glorify with the praise of your Lord and seek His forgiveness, for He is ever accepting of repentance} was revealed. This is the surah in which his noble death was announced to him, as Ibn 'Abbas stated explicitly, and 'Umar ibn al-Khattab agreed with him on this. A hadith has come regarding that which we shall relate when we come to its exegesis, and Allah knows best.

Abu Nu'aym also related it, from al-Tabarani, from Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Hadrami, from 'Ali ibn al-Husayn ibn Abi Burdah, from Yahya ibn Sa'id al-Aslami, from Harb ibn Sabih, from Sa'id ibn Maslamah, from Abu Murrah al-San'ani, from Abu 'Abd Allah al-Jadali, from Ibn Mas'ud, and he mentioned it, including in it the story of the appointment of a successor. This is a gharib chain of transmission and a strange narrative sequence.

Another route: The Imam Ahmad said: Abu Sa'id told us, Hammad ibn Salamah told us, from 'Ali ibn Zayd, from Abu Rafi', from Ibn Mas'ud, that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ drew a line around him, and each of them was like the blackness of bees, and he said to me, "Do not leave your place," and he recited to them the Book of Allah. When he saw the Zutt (a certain people), he said, "It is as if they resembled these." The Prophet ﷺ said, "Do you have water with you?" I said, "No." He said, "Do you have nabidh (date-water drink) with you?" I said, "Yes." So he performed ablution with it.

Another route, mursal (with a missing link at the beginning): Ibn Abi Hatim said: Abu 'Abd Allah al-Zahrani told us, Hafs ibn 'Umar al-'Adani informed us, al-Hakam ibn Aban told us, from 'Ikrimah, regarding the words of Allah Most High: {And when We directed toward you a company of the jinn}, he said: They were twelve thousand who came from the island of Mosul. The Prophet ﷺ said to Ibn Mas'ud, "Wait for me until I come to you," and he drew a line around him, and said, "Do not leave until I come to you." When Ibn Mas'ud feared them, he almost left, but he remembered the words of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and did not leave. The Prophet ﷺ said to him, "Had you left, we would not have met again until the Day of Resurrection."

Another route, also mursal: Sa'id ibn Abi 'Arubah said, from Qatadah, regarding the words of Allah Most High: {And when We directed toward you a company of the jinn}, he said: It has been mentioned to us that they were directed to him from Nineveh, and that the Prophet of Allah ﷺ said, "I have been commanded to recite to the jinn, so which of you will follow me?" They fell silent. He asked again, and they fell silent. He asked a third time, and a man said, "O Messenger of Allah, that one has a special calling," so Ibn Mas'ud, the brother of Hudhayl, followed him. He said: The Prophet ﷺ entered a mountain pass called "Shi'b al-Hajun," and drew a line around himself, and drew a line around Ibn Mas'ud to keep him fixed in place. He said: I began to be frightened, and I saw what looked like vultures walking along their edges, and I heard a great commotion, until I feared for the Prophet of Allah ﷺ. Then he recited the Qur'an. When the Messenger of Allah ﷺ returned, I said, "O Messenger of Allah, what was that commotion I heard?" He said, "They were disputing over a slain person, and judgment was passed between them with truth." Ibn Jarir and Ibn Abi Hatim related it.

All these various routes indicate that he ﷺ went to the jinn intentionally, recited the Qur'an to them, called them to Allah, Mighty and Majestic, and Allah legislated for them through his tongue what they needed at that time. It is possible that the first time they heard him reciting the Qur'an, he was not aware of them, as Ibn 'Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, said, and that afterward they came to him as a delegation, as Ibn Mas'ud related. As for Ibn Mas'ud, he was not with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ during the occasion when he addressed the jinn and called them, but was rather far from him, and no one went out with the Prophet ﷺ except him alone, yet even so he did not witness the occasion of the address. This is the approach of al-Bayhaqi.

It is also possible that the first time he went out to them, neither Ibn Mas'ud nor anyone else was with him, as is apparent from the wording of the first narration by way of Imam Ahmad, which is also found in Muslim. Then after that he went out with him another night, and Allah knows best, as Ibn Abi Hatim related in the exegesis of {Say, it has been revealed}, from the hadith of Ibn Jurayj, who said: 'Abd al-'Aziz ibn 'Umar said: As for the jinn who met him at Nakhlah, they were the jinn of Nineveh, and as for the jinn who met him at Makkah, they were the jinn of Nasibin. Al-Bayhaqi interpreted this by saying that he says, "We spent the worst night that any people ever spent," referring to someone other than Ibn Mas'ud, among those who did not know of his ﷺ going out to the jinn. This is possible, though somewhat remote, and Allah knows best.

The Hafiz Abu Bakr al-Bayhaqi said: Abu 'Amr Muhammad ibn 'Abd Allah al-Adib informed us, Abu Bakr al-Isma'ili informed us, al-Hasan ibn Sufyan informed us, Suwayd ibn Sa'id told me, 'Amr ibn Yahya told us, from his grandfather Sa'id ibn 'Amr, who said: Abu Hurayrah used to follow the Messenger of Allah ﷺ carrying a small water vessel for his ablution and his need. One day he caught up with him, and he said, "Who is this?" He said, "I am Abu Hurayrah." He said, "Bring me stones with which I can clean myself, and do not bring me a bone or dung." So I brought him stones in my garment, and placed them beside him. When he finished and stood up, I followed him and said, "O Messenger of Allah, what is the matter with bone and dung?" He said, "The delegation of the jinn of Nasibin came to me, and they asked me for provision, so I prayed to Allah for them that they would not pass by any bone or any dung without finding it to be food."

Al-Bukhari brought it out in his Sahih, from Musa ibn Isma'il, from 'Amr ibn Yahya, with a chain close to this. This indicates, along with what has preceded, that they came to him as a delegation after that. We shall mention what indicates the repetition of this.

Something other than what was first mentioned has been related from Ibn 'Abbas, by a sound route. Ibn Jarir said:

Abu Kurayb told us, 'Abd al-Hamid al-Himmani told us, al-Nadr ibn 'Arabi told us, from 'Ikrimah, from Ibn 'Abbas, regarding His words: {And when We directed toward you a company of the jinn}, the verse, [he said]: They were seven persons from the people of Nasibin, and the Messenger of Allah ﷺ made them messengers to their people.

This indicates that he related both stories.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: 'Ali ibn al-Husayn told us, Suwayd ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz told us, a man he named told us, from Ibn Jurayj, from Mujahid: {And when We directed toward you a company of the jinn}, the verse, he said: They were seven persons, three from the people of Harran and four from the people of Nasibin, and their names were Hayy, Hasy, and Masy, Shasir and Nasir, al-Ard, Ibyan, and al-Ahqam.

Abu Hamzah al-Thumali mentioned that this tribe of the jinn were called Banu al-Shaysaban, and that they were the most numerous of the jinn and the most noble in lineage, and that they constituted the majority of the armies of Iblis.

Sufyan al-Thawri said, from 'Asim, from Dharr, from Ibn Mas'ud: They were nine, one of them named Zawba'ah, and they came to him from the base of a palm tree at Nakhlah.

It has already been mentioned that they were fifteen, and in another report that they numbered sixty riding mounts, and it has already been mentioned that the name of their chief was Wardan, and it is also said that they were three hundred, and it has already been mentioned from Ikrimah that they were twelve thousand. Perhaps this discrepancy is evidence that their delegation came to him, upon him be the prayers and peace of Allah, more than once. Among what indicates this is what al-Bukhari said in his Sahih:

[chain] Yahya ibn Sulayman told us, Ibn Wahb told me, Umar (that is, Ibn Muhammad) told me, that Salim told him, from Abdullah ibn Umar, who said: I never heard Umar say of anything, "I truly think it is such and such," except that it turned out as he thought. While Umar ibn al-Khattab was sitting, a handsome man passed by him, and he said: "My guess has surely failed me, or this man was upon his old religion in the Jahiliyyah, or he was surely their kahin (soothsayer). Bring the man to me." So he was called for, and Umar said that to him. The man said: "I have never seen anything like today, that a Muslim man should be met with such a thing." Umar said: "I put you under solemn charge to tell me." He said: "I was their kahin in the Jahiliyyah." Umar said: "Then what is the most astonishing thing your jinn-familiar brought you?" He said: "One day while I was in the marketplace, she came to me and I could tell she was in terror, and she said:

Have you not seen the jinn and their despair, and their hopelessness after their downfall, and their attachment to riding camels and their saddle-cloths?"

Umar said: "He spoke the truth. While I was sleeping beside their idols, a man came with a calf and slaughtered it, and a crier cried out. I never heard a crier with a voice louder than his, saying: 'O Jalih, a successful matter! An eloquent man says: "There is no god but Allah."' The people leapt up, and I said: I will not leave until I know what lies behind this. Then he called out again: 'O Jalih, a successful matter! An eloquent man says: "There is no god but Allah."' So I got up, and it was not long before it was said: This is a prophet."

This is the wording of al-Bukhari. Al-Bayhaqi also related it through the hadith of Ibn Wahb, similarly, then said: "The apparent sense of this report gives the impression that Umar himself heard the crier crying out from the calf that was slaughtered, and this is likewise explicit in a weak report about Umar concerning his conversion to Islam. But the rest of the reports indicate that it was this kahin who reported that from what he had seen and heard, and Allah knows best."

What al-Bayhaqi said here is the correct approach, and this man was Sawad ibn Qarib. I have already given this in full detail in the biography of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, so whoever wants it may take it from there. To Allah belongs praise and grace.

Al-Bayhaqi said: "The hadith of Sawad ibn Qarib. It appears that this is the kahin whose name was not mentioned in the sound hadith."

[chain] Abu al-Qasim al-Hasan ibn Muhammad ibn Habib the exegete informed us from the source of his hearing, Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Saffar al-Asbahani informed us, by recitation to him, Abu Ja'far Ahmad ibn Musa al-Hammar al-Kufi told us in Kufa, Ziyad ibn Yazid ibn Badawayh Abu Bakr al-Qasri told us, Muhammad ibn Nawwas al-Kufi told us, Abu Bakr ibn Ayyash told us, from Abu Ishaq, from al-Bara [may Allah be pleased with him], who said: While Umar ibn al-Khattab was delivering a sermon to the people on the pulpit of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, he said: "O people, is Sawad ibn Qarib among you?" No one answered him that year. When the following year came, he said: "O people, is Sawad ibn Qarib among you?" I said: "O Commander of the Faithful, who is Sawad ibn Qarib?" Umar said to him: "The beginning of Sawad ibn Qarib's acceptance of Islam was a truly wondrous thing." He said: While we were like that, Sawad ibn Qarib appeared. Umar said to him: "O Sawad, tell us of the beginning of your Islam, how it happened." Sawad said: "I was residing in India, and I had a ra'i (jinn-familiar) among the jinn. One night while I was asleep, he came to me in that sleep of mine and said: 'Rise, understand, and comprehend if you can comprehend. A messenger has been sent from Luayy ibn Ghalib.' Then he began to recite:

I am amazed at the jinn and their impurity, and their fastening of the she-camels with their saddle-girths,

hastening to Mecca seeking guidance. The believers among the jinn are not like their wicked ones.

So rise to the chosen one of Hashim, and lift your eyes toward his head.

Then he woke me and startled me, and said: 'O Sawad ibn Qarib, Allah has sent a prophet, so rise to him, that you may be guided and rightly directed.' When the second night came, he came to me and woke me, then began reciting likewise:

I am amazed at the jinn and their seeking, and their fastening of the she-camels with their pack-saddles,

hastening to Mecca seeking guidance. Their vanguard is not like their rear.

So rise to the chosen one of Hashim, and lift your eyes toward his front tooth.

When the third night came, he came to me and woke me, then said:

I am amazed at the jinn and their news-seeking, and their fastening of the she-camels with their saddle-frames,

hastening to Mecca seeking guidance. The people of evil are not like their good ones.

So rise to the chosen one of Hashim. The believers among the jinn are not like their disbelievers.

When I heard this repeated night after night, love of Islam settled in my heart because of the matter of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, as much as Allah willed. So I went to my belongings and loaded them onto my riding mount, and I did not loosen one strap nor tie another until I came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. He was then in al-Madinah, meaning Mecca, and the people around him were as thick as a horse's mane. When the Prophet ﷺ saw me, he said: 'Welcome, O Sawad ibn Qarib. We already know what has brought you.' I said: 'O Messenger of Allah, I have composed some verses, so listen to them from me.'" Sawad said, so I said:

My familiar came to me after nights and a period of sleep, and in what I have tested he has never been a liar,

for three nights, saying each night: A messenger has come to you from Luayy ibn Ghalib.

So I rolled up my garment from my shin, and the sturdy, robust she-camel carried me across the open plains.

I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and that you are entrusted with every unseen matter,

and that you are nearest of the messengers in intercession before Allah, O son of the noblest and purest.

So command us with whatever comes to you, O best of messengers, even if what has come brings gray hair to the temples.

And be an intercessor for me on a day when no one but you can avail Sawad ibn Qarib with intercession.

He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ laughed until his molars showed, and said to me: "You have succeeded, O Sawad." Umar then said to him: "Does your familiar still come to you now?" He said: "Since I recited the Qur'an, he has not come to me, and the Book of Allah is an excellent substitute for the jinn."

Then al-Bayhaqi traced it with two other chains. Among what indicates their delegation coming to him, upon him be peace, after he emigrated to Madinah, is the hadith related by the hafiz Abu Nu'aym in his book "Dala'il al-Nubuwwah," where he said:

[chain] Sulayman ibn Ahmad told us, Muhammad ibn Abdah al-Missisi told us, Abu Tawbah al-Rabi' ibn Nafi' told us, Mu'awiyah ibn Sallam told us, from Zayd ibn Aslam, that he heard Abu Sallam say: someone told me that Amr ibn Ghaylan al-Thaqafi said: I came to Abdullah ibn Mas'ud and said to him: "I have been told that you were with the Messenger of Allah ﷺ on the night of the delegation of the jinn." He said: "Yes." I said: "Tell me how it happened." He said: "The People of the Suffah, each man of them was taken by another man to feed him for the evening, but I was left, and none of them took me. Then the Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed by me and said: 'Who is this?' I said: 'I am Ibn Mas'ud.' He said: 'Has no one taken you to feed you this evening?' I said: 'No.' He said: 'Then come along, perhaps I shall find something for you.' So we went until he came to the chamber of Umm Salamah. He left me and went in to his family. Then the servant girl came out and said: 'O Ibn Mas'ud, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ did not find any evening meal for you, so go back to your sleeping place.' So I went back to the mosque, gathered together the pebbles of the mosque and made a pillow of them, and wrapped myself in my garment. I had not waited long when the servant girl came and said: 'Answer the call of the Messenger of Allah.' So I followed her, hoping for the evening meal, until when I reached my place, the Messenger of Allah ﷺ came out with a palm-branch in his hand, and he held it up before my chest and said: 'Will you go with me wherever I go?' I said: 'As Allah wills.' He repeated it to me three times, each time I saying: 'As Allah wills.' Then he set off and I went with him, until we came to Baqi' al-Gharqad. He drew a line with his staff and said: 'Sit within it, and do not move from your place until I come to you.' Then he went off walking, and I watched him among the palm trees, until when he was where I could no longer see him, a black dust cloud rose up, and I was terrified, and I said: I must go to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, for I think that Hawazin has plotted against the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to kill him, and I will run to the houses and call the people for help."

So I remembered that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ had instructed me not to leave the place I was in. Then I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ striking them with his staff and saying: "Sit down." So they sat until the pillar of dawn nearly split, then they rose up and left. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ then came to me and said: "Did you sleep after I left?" I said: No, and indeed I was seized by that first fright, so much so that I thought of going to the houses and calling out to the people for help, until I heard you striking them with your staff. I had thought it was Hawazin, plotting against the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to kill him. He said: "Had you left this circle, I could not have guaranteed that some of them would not have snatched you away. Did you see anything of them?" I said: I saw black men wrapped in white garments. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: "Those were the delegation of the jinn of Nasibin. They came to me and asked me for provisions and goods, so I provided them with every dry, hollowed bone, and every dung of camel or animal droppings." I said: What good does that do them? He said: "They find no bone but that they find upon it the flesh it had on the day it was eaten, and no dung but that they find in it the grain that was in it on the day it was consumed. So none of you should clean yourselves with a bone or with dung."

This is an isnad that is extremely gharib (singular), but it contains an unnamed man who is not identified [and Allah knows best]. Al-Hafiz Abu Nu'aym related, from the hadith of Baqiyyah ibn al-Walid: [chain] Numayr ibn Zayd al-Qanbar told me, our father narrated to us, Quhafah ibn Rabi'ah narrated to us, al-Zubayr ibn al-Awwam told me, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ led us in the dawn prayer in the mosque of Madinah. When he finished, he said: "Which of you will follow me tonight to the delegation of the jinn?" The people remained silent three times. Then he passed by me and took my hand, and I began walking with him until all the mountains of Madinah were held back from us, and we came out onto open flat land. There were tall men, as if they were spears, wrapped in their garments from between their legs. When I saw them a violent trembling overcame me. Then he mentioned something similar to the previous hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. This is a gharib hadith, and Allah knows best.

Among what relates to the delegations of the jinn is what al-Hafiz Abu Nu'aym related: [chain] Abu Muhammad ibn Hayyan narrated to us, Abu al-Tayyib Ahmad ibn Rawh narrated to us, Ya'qub al-Dawraqi narrated to us, al-Walid ibn Bukayr al-Tamimi narrated to us, Husayn ibn Umar narrated to us, Ubayd al-Muktib informed me, from Ibrahim, who said: A group of the companions of Abdullah set out intending to perform the pilgrimage. When they were on part of the road, there was a white serpent coiling on the road, giving off a scent of musk. I said to my companions: Go on, I will not leave until I see what becomes of this serpent's affair. He said: It was not long before it died, so I took a white cloth and wrapped it in it, then moved it off the road and buried it. I caught up with my companions at the evening meal. He said: By Allah, we were sitting when four women approached from the direction of the west. One of them said: Which of you buried Amr? We said: Who is Amr? She said: Which of you buried the serpent? He said: I said: I did. She said: Indeed, by Allah, you have buried one who fasted much and prayed much, who used to command what Allah had revealed, and who had believed in your Prophet and heard a description of him from heaven four hundred years before he was sent as a prophet. The man said: We praised Allah, then we completed our pilgrimage. Then I passed by Umar ibn al-Khattab in Madinah and told him of the affair of the serpent. He said: You have spoken truly. I heard the Messenger of Allah ﷺ say: "He believed in me four hundred years before I was sent as a prophet."

This is an extremely gharib hadith, and Allah knows best.

Abu Nu'aym said: al-Thawri related from Abu Ishaq, from al-Sha'bi, from a man of Thaqif, something similar to it. Abdullah ibn Ahmad and al-Zahrani related from Safwan ibn al-Mu'attal, who is the one who dismounted and buried that serpent among the companions, and they said: Indeed, he was the last to die of the nine who came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ to listen to the Qur'an.

Abu Nu'aym related, from the hadith of al-Layth ibn Sa'd, from Abd al-Aziz ibn Abi Salamah al-Majishun, from his uncle, from Mu'adh ibn Ubaydullah ibn Ma'mar, who said: I was sitting with Uthman ibn Affan when a man came and said: O Commander of the Faithful, I was in an open expanse of land. He mentioned that he had seen two large serpents fighting each other, and then one killed the other. He said: I went to the place of the struggle and found many serpents killed, and a scent of musk was wafting from some of them. So I began smelling them one by one, until I found that scent coming from a thin yellow serpent. I wrapped it in my turban and buried it. As I was walking, a caller called out to me: O servant of Allah, you have been rightly guided! These are two tribes of the jinn, the Banu Ash'iban and the Banu Uqaysh, who fought each other, and among the slain was what you saw. The one you buried died as a martyr, and he was among those who heard the revelation from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ. He said: Uthman said to that man: If you are truthful, you have indeed seen something wondrous, and if you are lying, then the lie is upon you.

As for the saying of Allah, Exalted is He: {And when We directed toward you a company of the jinn}, meaning: a group of the jinn, {listening to the Qur'an, and when they came to it they said, "Listen attentively"}, meaning: pay heed, and this was a mark of proper conduct on their part.

Al-Hafiz al-Bayhaqi said: [chain] The Imam Abu al-Tayyib Sahl ibn Muhammad ibn Sulayman narrated to us, Abu al-Hasan Muhammad ibn Abdullah al-Daqqaq informed us, Muhammad ibn Ibrahim al-Bushanji narrated to us, Hisham ibn Ammar al-Dimashqi narrated to us, al-Walid ibn Muslim narrated to us, from Zuhayr ibn Muhammad, from Muhammad ibn al-Munkadir, from Jabir ibn Abdullah, who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ recited Surat al-Rahman until he completed it, then said: "What is it with me that I see you silent? The jinn gave a better response than you. Every time I recited to them this verse: {Then which of the favors of your Lord will you both deny?}, they said: Not any of Your favors, our Lord, do we deny, so to You belongs all praise."

Al-Tirmidhi related it in the Tafsir, from Abu Muslim Abd al-Rahman ibn Waqid, from al-Walid ibn Muslim, with the same chain. He said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ went out to his companions and recited to them Surat al-Rahman, and he mentioned it. Then al-Tirmidhi said: "Gharib, we do not know it except from the hadith of al-Walid, from Zuhayr." That is what he said. Al-Bayhaqi also related it from the hadith of Marwan ibn Muhammad al-Tatari, from Zuhayr ibn Muhammad, with the same chain, similarly.

As for His saying: {And when it was concluded}, meaning: it finished. Like His saying: {And when the prayer is concluded} [al-Jumu'ah: 10], {and He completed them as seven heavens in two days} [Fussilat: 12], {and when you have completed your rites} [al-Baqarah: 200]. {they turned back to their people, warning them}, meaning: they returned to their people and warned them of what they had heard from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, like His saying: {that they may learn deeply in religion and warn their people when they return to them, that they may take heed} [al-Tawbah: 122].

This verse has been used as evidence that among the jinn there are warners, but not messengers. There is no doubt that Allah did not send a messenger from among the jinn, because of His saying: {And We sent not before you except men to whom We gave revelation, from among the people of the towns} [Yusuf: 109], and He said: {And We did not send before you any of the messengers except that they ate food and walked in the markets} [al-Furqan: 20], and He said concerning Ibrahim the close friend (peace be upon him): {And We placed in his descendants prophethood and the Book} [al-Ankabut: 27].

So every prophet whom Allah sent after Ibrahim was from his descendants and lineage. As for His saying, Exalted is He, in [Surat] al-An'am: {O company of jinn and mankind, did there not come to you messengers from among you} [al-An'am: 130], what is meant is from the two kinds taken together, and it holds true if it applies to one of the two, namely mankind, just as in His saying: {From both of them emerge pearl and coral} [al-Rahman: 22], meaning: from one of the two. Then Allah, Exalted is He, explained the warning that the jinn gave to their people, saying, reporting about them: {They said, "O our people, indeed we have heard a Book revealed after Moses, confirming what came before it, guiding to the truth"}. They did not mention Jesus, because Jesus (peace be upon him) had the Gospel revealed to him, which contains exhortations and gentle admonitions and little of legal permission and prohibition, and it is in reality like a completion of the law of the Torah. So the Torah is the primary reference, and this is why they said: "revealed after Moses."

This is likewise what Waraqah ibn Nawfal said when the Prophet ﷺ told him the story of the first descent of Gabriel (peace be upon him) upon him. He said: "Bakh, bakh! This is the Namus (the divine messenger/angel) who used to come to Moses. Would that I might be a young man in it!"

{Confirming what came before it} means: of the books revealed before it to the prophets. Their statement, {It guides to the truth}, refers to belief and reports, and {and to a straight path} refers to deeds. For the Qur'an comprises two things: report and command. Its report is truthful and its command is just, as He said: {And the word of your Lord was completed in truth and justice} [al-An'am: 115], and He said: {It is He who sent His Messenger with guidance and the religion of truth} [al-Tawbah: 33]. So guidance is beneficial knowledge, and the religion of truth is righteous action. Likewise the jinn said: {It guides to the truth} in matters of belief, {and to a straight path} meaning in matters of action.

{O our people, respond to the caller of Allah}: this indicates that Allah, Exalted is He, sent Muhammad ﷺ, to the two weighty ones, mankind and jinn, in that he called them to Allah and recited to them the surah that contains address to both groups, their obligations, their promise and their warning, namely Surat al-Rahman. Therefore He said: {Respond to the caller of Allah and believe in Him.}

Regarding His statement, {He will forgive you some of your sins}: it has been said that "min" here is extra (grammatically superfluous), but there is reservation about this, since its addition in affirmative contexts is rare. It has also been said that it retains its original meaning of partitiveness. {And He will protect you from a painful punishment} means: He will shield you from His painful punishment.

Some scholars have used this verse as evidence that believing jinn do not enter Paradise, and that the reward of their righteous ones is only to be protected from the punishment of the Fire on the Day of Resurrection. They say this because this is a context of exultation and emphasis, and if there were a reward for their belief higher than this, they would have been quick to mention it.

Ibn Abi Hatim said: my father narrated to us, saying: I was told, from Jarir, from Layth, from Mujahid, from Ibn 'Abbas, who said: "The believing jinn do not enter Paradise, because they are of the offspring of Iblis, and the offspring of Iblis do not enter Paradise."

The truth is that their believers, like the believers among mankind, do enter Paradise, as is the position of a group of the early scholars (al-salaf). Some of them cited as evidence for this His statement: {Whom no man before them has touched, nor any jinn} [al-Rahman: 74], but there is reservation about this line of reasoning. Better than it is His statement, Exalted is He: {And for whoever fears the standing before his Lord are two gardens. Then which of the favors of your Lord will you both deny?} [al-Rahman: 46-47]. For Allah, Exalted is He, bestowed favor upon the two weighty ones by making the reward of the righteous among them Paradise, and the jinn responded to this verse with verbal gratitude more emphatically than mankind, saying: "And we do not deny any of Your favors, our Lord, so to You belongs all praise." Allah, Exalted is He, would not bestow favor upon them with a reward that they would not actually attain. Moreover, if He repays their disbelievers with the Fire, which is a matter of justice, then it is all the more fitting and appropriate that He repay their believers with Paradise, which is a matter of grace. Also indicating this is the general meaning of His statement, Exalted is He: {Indeed, those who believe and do righteous deeds, for them are the Gardens of Paradise as a lodging} [al-Kahf: 107], and similar verses. I have devoted a separate treatise to this question, and to Allah belongs all praise and grace. This Paradise continues to contain excess capacity until Allah brings into being a creation for it; will He then not settle in it whoever believed in Him and did righteous deeds for His sake? What they mentioned here as reward for belief, namely the expiation of sins and protection from painful punishment, necessarily entails entry into Paradise, because in the Hereafter there is nothing but Paradise or the Fire. Whoever is protected from the Fire enters Paradise without doubt. No explicit or even apparent text has reached us from the Lawgiver stating that believing jinn do not enter Paradise even if they are protected from the Fire, and had such a text been established as authentic, we would have adopted it. And Allah knows best. Here is Noah (peace be upon him) saying to his people: {He will forgive you some of your sins and delay you for an appointed term} [Nuh: 4], and there is no dispute that the believers among his people are in Paradise. The same applies to these jinn.

Strange opinions have been related concerning them. From 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz it is said that they do not enter the very heart of Paradise, but rather remain in its outskirts, around it, and in its outer regions. Some people have claimed that they are in Paradise such that the children of Adam see them but they do not see the children of Adam, the opposite of how things were in the worldly life. Others have said: they neither eat nor drink in Paradise, but rather are inspired to glorify, praise, and sanctify Allah instead of food and drink, like the angels, because they are of their kind. All these opinions have reservations about them, and there is no evidence for them.

Then He said, informing about him (Noah or the jinn speaker): {And whoever does not respond to the caller of Allah is not one who can escape on earth} meaning: rather, Allah's power encompasses him and surrounds him entirely, {and he has no protectors besides Him} meaning: no one can shield them from Him, {those are in manifest error}. This is a context of warning and intimidation. So they called their people with both enticement and warning, and this proved effective with many of them, and they came to the Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, in successive delegations, as has already been explained.

### Source (Arabic) — review against this

قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ، حَدَّثَنَا عَمْرٌو: سَمِعْتُ عِكْرِمَةَ، عَنِ الزُّبَيْرِ: ﴿وَإِذْ صَرَفْنَا إِلَيْكَ نَفَرًا مِنَ الْجِنِّ يَسْتَمِعُونَ الْقُرْآنَ﴾ قَالَ: بِنَخْلَةَ، وَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ يُصَلِّي الْعِشَاءَ الْآخِرَةَ، ﴿كَادُوا يَكُونُونَ عَلَيْهِ لِبَدًا﴾ [الْجِنِّ: ١٩] ، قَالَ سُفْيَانُ: اللِّبَدُ: بَعْضُهُمْ عَلَى بَعْضٍ، كَاللِّبَدِ بَعْضُهُ عَلَى بَعْضٍ .

تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ أَحْمَدُ، وَسَيَأْتِي مِنْ رِوَايَةِ ابْنِ جَرِيرٍ، عَنْ عِكْرِمَةَ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ: أَنَّهُمْ سَبْعَةٌ مِنْ جِنِّ نَصِيبين.

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَفَّانُ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَوَانَةَ (ح) -وَقَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي كِتَابِهِ "دَلَائِلِ النُّبُوَّةِ": أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو الْحَسَنِ عَلِيُّ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ عَبْدَانَ، أَخْبَرَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عُبَيْدٍ الصَّفَّارُ، حَدَّثَنَا إِسْمَاعِيلُ الْقَاضِي، أَخْبَرَنَا مُسَدَّدٌ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَوَانَةَ عَنْ أَبِي بِشْرٍ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: مَا قَرَأَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ عَلَى الْجِنِّ وَلَا رَآهُمْ، انْطَلَقَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فِي طَائِفَةٍ مِنْ أَصْحَابِهِ عَامِدِينَ إِلَى سُوقِ عُكَاظَ، وَقَدْ حِيلَ بَيْنَ الشَّيَاطِينِ وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ، وَأُرْسِلَتْ عَلَيْهِمُ الشُّهُبُ، فَرَجَعَتِ الشَّيَاطِينُ إِلَى قَوْمِهِمْ فَقَالُوا: مَا لَكُمْ؟ فَقَالُوا: حِيلَ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ، وَأُرْسِلَتْ عَلَيْنَا الشُّهُبُ. قَالُوا: مَا حَالَ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ إِلَّا شَيْءٌ حَدَثَ، فَاضْرِبُوا مَشَارِقَ الْأَرْضِ وَمَغَارِبَهَا وَانْظُرُوا مَا هَذَا الَّذِي حَالَ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ. فَانْطَلَقُوا يَضْرِبُونَ مَشَارِقَ الْأَرْضِ وَمَغَارِبَهَا يَبْتَغُونَ مَا هَذَا الَّذِي حَالَ بَيْنَهُمْ وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ، فَانْصَرَفَ أُولَئِكَ النَّفَرُ الَّذِينَ تَوَجَّهُوا نَحْوَ تِهَامَةَ إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَهُوَ بِنَخْلَةَ عَامِدًا إِلَى سُوقِ عُكَاظَ، وَهُوَ يُصَلِّي بِأَصْحَابِهِ صَلَاةَ الْفَجْرِ، فَلَمَّا سَمِعُوا الْقُرْآنَ اسْتَمَعُوا لَهُ، فَقَالُوا: هَذَا -وَاللَّهِ-الَّذِي حَالَ بَيْنَكُمْ وَبَيْنَ خَبَرِ السَّمَاءِ، فَهُنَالِكَ حِينَ رَجَعُوا إِلَى قَوْمِهِمْ، قَالُوا: يَا قَوْمَنَا، إِنَّا سَمِعْنَا قُرْآنًا عَجَبًا، يَهْدِي إِلَى الرُّشْدِ فَآمَنَّا بِهِ، وَلَنْ نُشْرِكَ بِرَبِّنَا أَحَدًا، وَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَى نَبِيِّهِ : ﴿قُلْ أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ أَنَّهُ اسْتَمَعَ نَفَرٌ مِنَ الْجِنِّ﴾ [الْجِنِّ: ١] ، وَإِنَّمَا أُوحِيَ إِلَيْهِ قَوْلُ الْجِنِّ.

رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ عَنْ مُسَدَّد بِنَحْوِهِ، وَأَخْرَجَهُ مُسْلِمٌ عَنْ شَيْبَانَ بْنِ فَرُّوخَ، عَنْ أبي عوانة، به. ورواه التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ فِي التَّفْسِيرِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ أَبِي عَوَانَةَ .

وَقَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو أحمد، حدثنا إِسْرَائِيلُ، عَنْ أَبِي إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ ، عن ابن عباس، قال: كَانَ الْجِنُّ يَسْتَمِعُونَ الْوَحْيَ، فَيَسْمَعُونَ الْكَلِمَةَ فَيَزِيدُونَ فِيهَا عَشْرًا، فَيَكُونُ مَا سَمِعُوا حَقًّا وَمَا زَادُوا بَاطِلًا وَكَانَتِ النُّجُومُ لَا يُرْمَى بِهَا قَبْلَ ذَلِكَ، فَلَمَّا بُعِثَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ لَا يَأْتِي مَقْعَدَهُ إِلَّا رُمِيَ بِشِهَابٍ يَحْرِقُ مَا أَصَابَ، فَشَكَوْا ذَلِكَ إِلَى إِبْلِيسَ فَقَالَ: مَا هَذَا إِلَّا مِنْ أَمْرٍ قَدْ حَدَثَ. فَبَثَّ جُنُودَهُ، فَإِذَا بِالنَّبِيِّ ﷺ يُصَلِّي بَيْنَ جَبَلَيْ نَخْلَةَ، فَأَتَوْهُ فَأَخْبَرُوهُ، فَقَالَ: هَذَا الْحَدَثُ الَّذِي حَدَثَ فِي الْأَرْضِ.

وَرَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَالنَّسَائِيُّ فِي كِتَابَيِ التَّفْسِيرِ مِنْ سُنَنَيْهِمَا، مِنْ حَدِيثِ إِسْرَائِيلَ بِهِ وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: حَسَنٌ صَحِيحٌ.

وَهَكَذَا رَوَاهُ أَيُّوبَ عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ جُبَيْرٍ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ. وَكَذَا رَوَاهُ الْعَوْفِيُّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ أَيْضًا، بِمِثْلِ هَذَا السِّيَاقِ بِطُولِهِ، وَهَكَذَا قَالَ الْحَسَنُ الْبَصْرِيُّ: إِنَّهُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، مَا شَعَرَ بِأَمْرِهِمْ حَتَّى أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ بِخَبَرِهِمْ.

وَذَكَرَ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ إِسْحَاقَ، عَنْ يَزِيدَ بْنِ رُومَانَ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ كَعْبٍ الْقُرَظِيِّ قِصَّةَ خُرُوجِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ إِلَى الطَّائِفِ وَدُعَائِهِ إِيَّاهُمْ إِلَى اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، وَإِبَائِهِمْ عَلَيْهِ. فَذَكَرَ الْقِصَّةَ بِطُولِهَا، وَأَوْرَدَ ذَلِكَ الدُّعَاءَ الْحَسَنَ: "اللَّهُمَّ إِلَيْكَ أَشْكُو ضَعْفَ قُوَّتِي وَقِلَّةَ حِيلَتِي" إِلَى آخِرِهِ. قَالَ: فَلَمَّا انْصَرَفَ عَنْهُمْ بَاتَ بِنَخْلَةَ، فَقَرَأَ تِلْكَ اللَّيْلَةَ مِنَ الْقُرْآنِ فَاسْتَمَعَهُ الْجِنُّ مِنْ أَهْلِ نَصِيبِينَ .

وَهَذَا صَحِيحٌ، وَلَكِنَّ قَوْلَهُ: "إِنَّ الْجِنَّ كَانَ اسْتِمَاعُهُمْ تِلْكَ اللَّيْلَةَ". فِيهِ نَظَرٌ؛ لِأَنَّ الْجِنَّ كَانَ اسْتِمَاعُهُمْ فِي ابْتِدَاءِ الْإِيحَاءِ، كَمَا دَلَّ عَلَيْهِ حَدِيثُ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ الْمَذْكُورُ، وَخُرُوجُهُ، عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ، إِلَى الطَّائِفِ كَانَ بَعْدَ مَوْتِ عَمِّهِ، وَذَلِكَ قَبْلَ الْهِجْرَةِ بِسَنَةٍ أَوْ سَنَتَيْنِ، كَمَا قَرَّرَهُ ابْنُ إِسْحَاقَ وَغَيْرُهُ [وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ] .

وَقَالَ أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو أَحْمَدَ الزُّبَيْرِيُّ، حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانَ، عَنْ عَاصِمٍ، عَنْ زِرٍّ ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: هَبَطُوا عَلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ وَهُوَ يَقْرَأُ الْقُرْآنَ بِبَطْنِ نَخْلَةَ، فَلَمَّا سَمِعُوهُ قَالُوا: أَنْصِتُوا. قَالَ صَهٍ، وَكَانُوا تِسْعَةً أَحَدُهُمْ زَوْبَعَةُ، فَأَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ: ﴿وَإِذْ صَرَفْنَا إِلَيْكَ نَفَرًا مِنَ الْجِنِّ يَسْتَمِعُونَ الْقُرْآنَ فَلَمَّا حَضَرُوهُ قَالُوا أَنْصِتُوا فَلَمَّا قُضِيَ وَلَّوْا إِلَى قَوْمِهِمْ مُنْذِرِينَ﴾ إلى: ﴿ضَلالٍ مُبِينٍ﴾ .

فَهَذَا مَعَ الْأَوَّلِ مِنْ رِوَايَةِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ يَقْتَضِي أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَمْ يَشْعُرْ بِحُضُورِهِمْ فِي هَذِهِ الْمَرَّةِ وَإِنَّمَا اسْتَمَعُوا قِرَاءَتَهُ، ثُمَّ رَجَعُوا إِلَى قَوْمِهِمْ ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ وَفَدُوا إِلَيْهِ أَرْسَالًا قَوْمًا بَعْدَ قَوْمٍ، وَفَوْجًا بَعْدَ فَوْجٍ، كَمَا سَيَأْتِي بِذَلِكَ الْأَخْبَارُ فِي مَوْضِعِهَا وَالْآثَارُ، مِمَّا سَنُورِدُهَا هَاهُنَا إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى وَبِهِ الثِّقَةُ.

فَأَمَّا مَا رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ وَمُسْلِمٌ جَمِيعًا، عَنْ أَبِي قُدَامَةَ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ سَعِيدٍ السَّرْخَسِيِّ، عَنْ أَبِي أُسَامَةَ حَمَّادِ بْنِ أُسَامَةَ، عَنْ مِسْعَرُ بْنُ كِدَامٍ، عَنْ مَعْنِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ أَبِي قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ مَسْرُوقًا: مَنْ آذَنَ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ اسْتَمَعُوا الْقُرْآنَ؟ فَقَالَ: حَدَّثَنِي أَبُوكَ -يَعْنِي ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ -أَنَّهُ آذَنَتْهُ بِهِمْ شَجَرَةٌ -فَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَذَا فِي الْمَرَّةِ الْأُولَى، وَيَكُونُ إِثْبَاتًا مُقَدَّمًا عَلَى نَفْيِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ هَذَا فِي بَعْضِ الْمَرَّاتِ الْمُتَأَخِّرَاتِ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ. وَيُحْتَمَلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي الْأُولَى وَلَكِنْ لَمْ يَشْعُرْ بِهِمْ حَالَ اسْتِمَاعِهِمْ حَتَّى آذَنَتْهُ بِهِمُ الشَّجَرَةُ، أَيْ: أَعْلَمَتْهُ بِاسْتِمَاعِهِمْ، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ.

قَالَ الْحَافِظُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ: وَهَذَا الَّذِي حَكَاهُ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا ، إِنَّمَا هُوَ فِي أَوَّلِ مَا سَمِعَتِ الْجِنُّ قِرَاءَةَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَعَلِمَتْ حَالَهُ، وَفِي ذَلِكَ الْوَقْتِ لَمْ يَقْرَأْ عَلَيْهِمْ وَلَمْ يَرَهُمْ، ثُمَّ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ أَتَاهُ دَاعِي الْجِنِّ فَقَرَأَ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْآنَ، وَدَعَاهُمْ إِلَى اللَّهِ، عَزَّ وَجَلَّ، كَمَا رَوَاهُ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ .

ذَكَرَ الرِّوَايَةِ عَنْهُ بِذَلِكَ:

قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا إِسْمَاعِيلُ بْنُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ، حَدَّثَنَا دَاوُدُ عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ -وَابْنُ أَبِي زَائِدَةَ، أَخْبَرَنَا دَاوُدُ، عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ -عَنْ عَلْقَمَةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِعَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ: هَلْ صَحِبَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةُ الْجِنِّ مِنْكُمْ أَحَدٌ؟ فَقَالَ: مَا صَحِبَهُ مِنَّا أَحَدٌ، وَلَكِنَّا فَقَدْنَاهُ ذَاتَ لَيْلَةٍ بِمَكَّةَ، فَقُلْنَا: اغْتِيلَ؟ اسْتُطِيرَ؟ مَا فَعَلَ؟ قَالَ: فَبِتْنَا بِشَرِّ لَيْلَةٍ بَاتَ بِهَا قَوْمٌ، فَلَمَّا كَانَ فِي وَجْهِ الصُّبْحِ -أَوْ قَالَ: فِي السَّحَرِ-إِذَا نَحْنُ بِهِ يَجِيءُ مِنْ قِبَلِ حِرَاءٍ، فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ -فَذَكَرُوا لَهُ الَّذِي كَانُوا فِيهِ-فَقَالَ: "إِنَّهُ أَتَانِي دَاعِي الْجِنِّ، فَأَتَيْتُهُمْ فَقَرَأْتُ عَلَيْهِمْ". قَالَ: فَانْطَلَقَ، فَأَرَانَا آثَارَهُمْ وَآثَارَ نِيرَانِهِمْ -قَالَ: وَقَالَ الشَّعْبِيُّ: سَأَلُوهُ الزَّادَ-قَالَ عَامِرٌ: سَأَلُوهُ بِمَكَّةَ، وَكَانُوا مِنْ جِنِّ الْجَزِيرَةِ، فَقَالَ: "كُلُّ عَظْمٍ ذُكِرَ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ يَقَعُ فِي أَيْدِيكُمْ أَوْفَرَ مَا كَانَ عَلَيْهِ لَحْمًا، وَكُلُّ بَعْرَةٍ أَوْ رَوْثَةٍ عَلَفٌ لِدَوَابِّكُمْ -قَالَ-فَلَا تَسْتَنْجُوا بِهِمَا، فَإِنَّهُمَا زَادُ إِخْوَانِكُمْ مِنَ الْجِنِّ".

وَهَكَذَا رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ فِي صَحِيحِهِ، عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ حُجْرٍ، عَنْ إِسْمَاعِيلَ بْنِ عُلَيَّةَ، بِهِ نَحْوَهُ .

وَقَالَ مُسْلِمٌ أَيْضًا: حَدَّثَنَا مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ الْمُثَنَّى، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الْأَعْلَى، حَدَّثَنَا دَاوُدُ -وَهُوَ ابْنُ أَبِي هِنْدٍ-عَنْ عَامِرٍ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ عَلْقَمَةَ: هَلْ كَانَ ابْنُ مَسْعُودٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، شَهِدَ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ ليلة الْجِنِّ؟ قَالَ: فَقَالَ عَلْقَمَةُ: أَنَا سَأَلْتُ ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ؛ فَقُلْتُ: هَلْ شَهِدَ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ ليلة الْجِنِّ؟ قَالَ: لَا وَلَكِنَّا كُنَّا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ ذَاتَ لَيْلَةٍ فَفَقَدْنَاهُ فَالْتَمَسْنَاهُ فِي الْأَوْدِيَةِ وَالشِّعَابِ، فَقُلْنَا: اسْتُطِيرَ؟ اغْتِيلَ؟ قَالَ: فَبِتْنَا بِشَرِّ لَيْلَةٍ بَاتَ بِهَا قَوْمٌ، فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحْنَا إِذَا هُوَ جَاءَ مِنْ قِبَلِ حِرَاءٍ، قَالَ: فَقُلْنَا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَقَدْنَاكَ فَطَلَبْنَاكَ فَلَمْ نَجِدْكَ، فَبِتْنَا بِشَرِّ لَيْلَةٍ بَاتَ بِهَا قَوْمٌ. فَقَالَ: "أَتَانِي دَاعِي الْجِنِّ، فَذَهَبْتُ مَعَهُمْ، فَقَرَأْتُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْآنَ". قَالَ: فَانْطَلَقَ بِنَا فَأَرَانَا آثَارَهُمْ وَآثَارَ نِيرَانِهِمْ، وَسَأَلُوهُ الزَّادَ فَقَالَ: "كُلُّ عَظْمٍ ذُكِرَ اسْمُ اللَّهِ عَلَيْهِ يَقَعُ فِي أَيْدِيكُمْ أَوْفَرَ مَا يَكُونُ لَحْمًا، وَكُلُّ بَعْرَةٍ أَوْ رَوْثَةٍ عَلَفٌ لِدَوَابِّكُمْ". قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: "فَلَا تَسْتَنْجُوا بِهِمَا، فَإِنَّهُمَا طَعَامُ إِخْوَانِكُمْ" .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ: قَالَ أَبُو جَعْفَرِ بْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنِي أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ، حَدَّثَنِي عَمِّي، حَدَّثَنِي يُونُسُ، عَنِ الزُّهْرِيِّ، عَنْ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ؛ أن بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: "بِتُّ اللَّيْلَةَ أَقْرَأُ عَلَى الْجِنِّ رُبْعًا بِالْحَجُونِ" .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: فِيهَا أَنَّهُ كَانَ مَعَهُ لَيْلَةَ الْجِنِّ، قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ: حَدَّثَنِي أَحْمَدُ بْنُ عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ بْنِ وَهْبٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَمِّي عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ وَهْبٍ، أَخْبَرَنِي يُونُسُ، عَنِ ابْنِ شِهَابٍ، عَنْ أَبِي عُثْمَانَ بْنِ سَنَّةَ الْخُزَاعِيِّ -وَكَانَ مِنْ أَهْلِ الشَّامِ -أَنَّ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ لِأَصْحَابِهِ وَهُوَ بِمَكَّةَ: "مَنْ أَحَبَّ مِنْكُمْ أَنْ يَحْضُرَ أَمْرَ الْجِنِّ اللَّيْلَةَ فَلْيَفْعَلْ". فَلَمْ يَحْضُرْ مِنْهُمْ أَحَدٌ غَيْرِي، قَالَ: فَانْطَلَقْنَا حَتَّى إِذَا كُنَّا بِأَعْلَى مَكَّةَ خَطَّ لِي بِرِجْلِهِ خَطًّا، ثُمَّ أَمَرَنِي أَنْ أَجْلِسَ فِيهِ، ثُمَّ انْطَلَقَ حَتَّى قَامَ، فَافْتَتَحَ الْقُرْآنَ فَغَشِيَتْهُ أَسْوِدَةٌ كَثِيرَةٌ حَالَتْ بَيْنِي وَبَيْنَهُ، حَتَّى مَا أَسْمَعُ صَوْتَهُ، ثُمَّ طَفِقُوا يَتَقَطَّعُونَ مِثْلَ قِطَعِ السَّحَابِ ذَاهِبِينَ، حَتَّى بَقِيَ مِنْهُمْ رَهْطٌ، فَفَرَغَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ مَعَ الْفَجْرِ، فَانْطَلَقَ فَتَبَرَّزَ، ثُمَّ أَتَانِي فَقَالَ: "مَا فَعَلَ الرَّهْطُ؟ " فَقُلْتُ: هُمْ أُولَئِكَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَأَعْطَاهُمْ عَظْمًا وَرَوْثًا زَادًا، ثُمَّ نَهَى أَنْ يَسْتَطِيبَ أَحَدٌ بِرَوْثٍ أَوْ عَظْمٍ.

وَرَوَاهُ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْحَكَمِ، عَنْ أَبِي زُرْعَةَ وَهْبِ اللَّهِ بْنِ رَاشِدٍ، عَنْ يُونُسَ بْنِ يَزِيدَ الْأَيْلِيِّ، بِهِ .

وَرَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي الدَّلَائِلِ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ صَالِحٍ -كَاتِبِ اللَّيْثِ-عَنِ اللَّيْثِ، عَنْ يُونُسَ بِهِ .

وَقَدْ رَوَى إِسْحَاقُ بْنُ رَاهَوَيْهِ، عَنْ جَرِيرٌ، عَنْ قَابُوسُ بْنُ أَبِي ظَبْيَانَ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ ابن مسعود، فذكر نحو ما تقدم .

وَرَوَاهُ الْحَافِظُ أَبُوُ نُعَيْمٍ، مِنْ طَرِيقِ مُوسَى بْنِ عُبَيْدَةَ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ الْحَارِثِ، عَنْ أَبِي الْمُعَلَّى ، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ فَذَكَرَ نَحْوَهُ أَيْضًا .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ مَالِكٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ حَنْبَلٍ، حَدَّثَنِي أَبِي قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا عَفَّانُ وَعِكْرِمَةُ قَالَا حَدَّثَنَا مُعْتَمِرٌ قَالَ: قَالَ أَبِي: حَدَّثَنِي أَبُو تَمِيمَةَ، عَنْ عَمْرٍو -وَلَعَلَّهُ قَدْ يَكُونُ قَالَ: الْبِكَالِيُّ-يُحَدِّثُهُ عَمْرٌو، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، قَالَ: اسْتَتْبَعَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَانْطَلَقْنَا حَتَّى أَتَيْنَا مَكَانَ كَذَا وَكَذَا، فَخَطَّ لِي خَطًّا فَقَالَ: "كُنْ بَيْنَ ظَهْرِ هَذِهِ لَا تَخْرُجُ مِنْهَا؛ فَإِنَّكَ إِنْ خَرَجْتَ مِنْهَا هَلَكْتَ" فَذَكَرَ الْحَدِيثَ بِطُولِهِ وَفِيهِ غَرَابَةٌ شَدِيدَةٌ .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ ابْنُ جَرِيرٍ: حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ عَبْدِ الْأَعْلَى، حَدَّثَنَا ابْنُ ثَوْرٍ، عَنْ مَعْمَرٌ، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ أَبِي كَثِيرٍ ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَمْرٍو بْنِ غَيْلَانَ الثَّقَفِيِّ؛ أَنَّهُ قَالَ لِابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ: حُدِّثْتُ أَنَّكَ كُنْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ وَفْدِ الْجِنِّ؟ قَالَ: أَجَلْ. قَالَ: فَكَيْفَ كَانَ؟ فَذَكَرَ الْحَدِيثَ كُلَّهُ، وَذَكَرَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ خَطَّ عَلَيْهِ خَطًّا، وَقَالَ: "لَا تَبْرَحْ مِنْهَا" فَذَكَرَ مِثْلَ العَجَاجة السَّوْدَاءِ غَشِيَتْ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَذُعِرَ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ، حَتَّى إِذَا كَانَ قَرِيبًا مِنَ الصُّبْحِ، أَتَانِي النَّبِيُّ ﷺ فَقَالَ: "أَنِمْتَ؟ " فَقُلْتُ: لَا وَاللَّهِ، وَلَقَدْ هَمَمْتُ مِرَارًا أَنْ أَسْتَغِيثَ بِالنَّاسِ حَتَّى سَمِعْتُكَ تُقَرِّعُهُمْ بِعَصَاكَ، تَقُولُ: "اجْلِسُوا" فَقَالَ: "لَوْ خَرَجْتَ لَمْ آمَنْ أَنْ يَخْطَفَكَ بَعْضُهُمْ". ثُمَّ قَالَ: "هَلْ رَأَيْتَ شَيْئًا؟ " فَقُلْتُ: نَعَمْ رَأَيْتُ رِجَالًا سُودًا مُسْتَشْعِرِينَ ثِيَابًا بَيَاضًا. قَالَ: "أُولَئِكَ جِنُّ نَصِيبِينَ سَأَلُونِي الْمَتَاعَ -وَالْمَتَاعُ: الزَّادُ-فَمَتَّعْتُهُمْ بِكُلِّ عَظْمٍ حَائِلٍ، أَوْ بَعْرَةٍ أَوْ رَوْثَةٍ"-فَقُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، وَمَا يُغْنِي ذَلِكَ عَنْهُمْ؟ فَقَالَ: "إِنَّهُمْ لَا يَجِدُونَ عَظْمًا إِلَّا وَجَدُوا عَلَيْهِ لَحْمَهُ يَوْمَ أُكِلَ، وَلَا رَوْثًا إِلَّا وَجَدُوا فِيهَا حَبَّهَا يَوْمَ أُكِلَتْ، فَلَا يَسْتَنْقِيَنَّ أَحَدٌ مِنْكُمْ إِذَا خَرَجَ مِنَ الْخَلَاءِ بِعَظْمٍ وَلَا بَعْرَةٍ وَلَا رَوْثَةٍ" .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو بَكْرٍ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ: أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو عَبْدِ الرَّحْمَنِ السُّلَمِيُّ وَأَبُو نَصْرِ بْنُ قَتَادَةُ قَالَا أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو مُحَمَّدٍ يَحْيَى بْنُ مَنْصُورٍ الْقَاضِي، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو عَبْدِ اللَّهِ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ البُوشَنْجي، حَدَّثَنَا رَوْحُ بْنُ صَلَاحٍ، حَدَّثَنَا مُوسَى بْنُ عَلِيِّ بْنِ رَبَاحٍ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: اسْتَتْبَعَنِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَقَالَ: "إِنَّ نَفَرًا مِنَ الْجِنِّ -خَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ بَنِي إِخْوَةٍ وَبَنِي عَمٍّ-يَأْتُونَنِي اللَّيْلَةَ، فَأَقْرَأُ عَلَيْهِمُ الْقُرْآنَ"، فَانْطَلَقْتُ مَعَهُ إِلَى الْمَكَانِ الَّذِي أَرَادَ، فَخَطَّ لِي خَطًّا وَأَجْلَسَنِي فِيهِ، وَقَالَ لِي: "لَا تَخْرُجْ مِنْ هَذَا". فَبِتُّ فِيهِ حَتَّى أَتَانِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ مَعَ السَّحَرِ فِي يَدِهِ عَظْمٌ حَائِلٌ وَرَوْثَةٌ حُمَمة فَقَالَ لِي: "إِذَا ذَهَبْتَ إِلَى الْخَلَاءِ فَلَا تَسْتَنْجِ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ هَؤُلَاءِ". قَالَ: فَلَمَّا أَصْبَحْتُ قُلْتُ: لَأَعْلَمَنَّ عِلْمِي حَيْثُ كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ قال، فَذَهَبْتُ فَرَأَيْتُ مَوْضِعَ مَبْرِكِ سِتِّينَ بَعِيرًا .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ: أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْحَافِظُ، أَخْبَرْنَا أَبُو الْعَبَّاسِ الْأَصَمُّ، حَدَّثَنَا الْعَبَّاسُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدٍ الدُّوري، حَدَّثَنَا عُثْمَانُ بْنُ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ الْمُسْتَمِرِّ بْنِ الرَّيَّانِ، عَنْ أَبِي الْجَوْزَاءِ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: انْطَلَقْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ الْجِنِّ، حَتَّى أَتَى الْحَجُونَ، فَخَطَّ لِي خَطًّا، ثُمَّ تَقَدَّمَ إِلَيْهِمْ فَازْدَحَمُوا عَلَيْهِ، فَقَالَ سَيِّدٌ لَهُمْ يُقَالُ لَهُ: "وَرْدَانُ": أَنَا أُرَحِّلُهُمْ عَنْكَ. فَقَالَ: إِنِّي لَنْ يُجِيرَنِي مِنَ اللَّهِ أَحَدٌ .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، حَدَّثَنَا سُفْيَانُ، عَنْ أَبِي فَزَارَةَ الْعَبْسِيِّ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو زَيْدٍ -مَوْلَى عَمْرِو بْنِ حُرَيْثٍ-عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: لَمَّا كَانَ لَيْلَةُ الْجِنِّ قَالَ لِيَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "أَمَعَكَ مَاءٌ؟ " قُلْتُ: لَيْسَ مَعِيَ مَاءٌ، وَلَكِنَّ مَعِيَ إِدَاوَةً فِيهَا نَبِيذٌ. فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ: "تَمْرَةٌ طَيِّبَةٌ وَمَاءٌ طَهُورٌ" فَتَوَضَّأَ.

وَرَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ، وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ، مِنْ حَدِيثِ أَبِي زَيْدٍ، بِهِ .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا يَحْيَى بْنُ إِسْحَاقَ، أَخْبَرَنَا ابْنُ لَهِيعَةَ، عَنْ قَيْسِ بْنِ الْحَجَّاجِ، عَنْ حَنَشٍ الصَّنْعَانِيِّ، عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ؛ أَنَّهُ كَانَ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ الْجِنِّ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ: "يَا عَبْدَ اللَّهِ، أَمَعَكَ مَاءٌ؟ " قَالَ: مَعِيَ نَبِيذٌ فِي إِدَاوَةٍ، فَقَالَ اصْبُبْ عَلَيَّ". فَتَوَضَّأَ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: "يَا عَبْدَ اللَّهِ شَرَابٌ وَطَهُورٌ" .

تَفَرَّدَ بِهِ أَحْمَدُ مِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ، وَقَدْ أَوْرَدَهُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيُّ مِنْ طَرِيقٍ آخَرَ، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، [بِهِ] .

طَرِيقٌ أُخْرَى: قَالَ الْإِمَامُ أَحْمَدُ: حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، أَخْبَرَنِي أَبِي عَنْ مِينَاءَ، عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ قَالَ: كُنْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ وَفْدِ الْجِنِّ، فَلَمَّا انْصَرَفَ تَنَفَّسَ، فَقُلْتُ: مَا شَأْنُكَ؟ قَالَ: "نُعِيَتْ إِلَيَّ نَفْسِي يَا ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ".

هَكَذَا رَأَيْتُهُ فِي الْمُسْنَدِ مُخْتَصَرًا ، وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ الْحَافِظُ أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ فِي كِتَابِهِ "دَلَائِلُ النُّبُوَّةِ"، فَقَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا سُلَيْمَانُ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ أَيُّوبَ، حَدَّثَنَا إِسْحَاقُ بْنُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ -وَحَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ مَالِكٍ، حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ أَحْمَدَ بْنِ حَنْبَلٍ، حَدَّثَنَا أَبِي قَالَا حَدَّثَنَا عَبْدُ الرَّزَّاقِ، عَنْ أَبِيهِ، عَنْ مِينَاءَ، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ قَالَ: كُنْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ لَيْلَةَ وَفْدِ الْجِنِّ، فَتَنَفَّسَ، فَقُلْتُ: مَا لَكَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: "نُعِيَتْ إِلَيَّ نَفْسِي يَا ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ". قُلْتُ: اسْتَخْلِفْ. قَالَ: "مَنْ؟ " قُلْتُ: أَبَا بَكْرٍ. فَسَكَتَ ، ثُمَّ مَضَى سَاعَةً فَتَنَفَّسَ، فَقُلْتُ: مَا شَأْنُكَ بِأَبِي أَنْتَ وَأُمِّي يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: "نُعِيَتْ إِلَيَّ نَفْسِي يَا ابْنَ مَسْعُودٍ". قُلْتُ: اسْتَخْلِفْ. قَالَ: "مَنْ؟ " قُلْتُ: عُمَرَ [بْنَ الْخَطَّابِ] . فَسَكَتَ، ثُمَّ مَضَى سَاعَةً، ثُمَّ تَنَفَّسَ فَقُلْتُ: مَا شَأْنُكَ؟ قَالَ: "نُعِيَتْ إِلَيَّ نَفْسِي". قُلْتُ: فَاسْتَخْلِفْ. قَالَ ﷺ: "مَنْ؟ " قُلْتُ: عَلِيَّ بْنَ أَبِي طَالِبٍ. قَالَ ﷺ: "أَمَّا وَالَّذِي نَفْسِي بِيَدِهِ، لَئِنْ أَطَاعُوهُ ليدخلن الجنة أجمعين أكتعين. .

وَهُوَ حَدِيثٌ غَرِيبٌ جِدًّا، وَأَحْرَى بِهِ أَلَّا يَكُونَ مَحْفُوظًا، وَبِتَقْدِيرِ صِحَّتِهِ فَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّ هَذَا بَعْدَ وُفُودِهِمْ إِلَيْهِ بِالْمَدِينَةِ عَلَى مَا سَنُورِدُهُ، فَإِنَّ فِي ذَلِكَ الْوَقْتِ فِي آخِرِ الْأَمْرِ لَمَّا فُتِحَتْ مَكَّةُ، وَدَخَلَ النَّاسُ وَالْجَانُّ أَيْضًا فِي دِينِ اللَّهِ أَفْوَاجًا، نَزَلَتْ سُورَةُ ﴿إِذَا جَاءَ نَصْرُ اللَّهِ وَالْفَتْحُ. وَرَأَيْتَ النَّاسَ يَدْخُلُونَ فِي دِينِ اللَّهِ أَفْوَاجًا. فَسَبِّحْ بِحَمْدِ رَبِّكَ وَاسْتَغْفِرْهُ إِنَّهُ كَانَ تَوَّابًا﴾ ، وَهِيَ السُّورَةُ الَّتِي نُعِيَتْ نَفْسُهُ الْكَرِيمَةُ فِيهَا إِلَيْهِ، كَمَا قَدْ نَصَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ ابْنُ عَبَّاسٍ، وَوَافَقَهُ عُمَرُ بْنُ الْخَطَّابِ عَلَيْهِ، وَقَدْ وَرَدَ فِي ذَلِكَ حَدِيثٌ سَنُورِدُهُ عِنْدَ تَفْسِيرِهَا، وَاللَّهُ أَعْلَمُ. وَقَدْ رَوَاهُ أَبُو نُعَيْمٍ أَيْضًا، عَنِ الطَّبَرَانِيِّ، عَنْ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْحَضْرَمِيِّ، عَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ الْحُسَيْنِ بْنِ أَبِي بُرْدَةَ، عَنْ يَحْيَى بْنِ سَعِيدٍ الْأَسْلَمَيِّ، عَنْ حَرْبِ بْنِ صَبِيح، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ مَسْلَمَةَ، عَنْ أَبِي مُرَّةَ الصَّنْعَانِيِّ، عَنْ أَبِي عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْجَدَلِيِّ، عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ، فَذَكَرَهُ وَذَكَرَ فِيهِ قِصَّةَ الِاسْتِخْلَافِ ، وَهَذَا إِسْنَادٌ غَرِيبٌ، وَسِيَاقٌ عَجِيبٌ.
